1. 
TEST DELIVERABLES AND REPORTING REQUIREMENTS 
 
1.1 
MONTHLY STATUS REPORTS 
 
A. 
MONTHLY VEHICLE INVENTORY REPORT 
 
The Contractor shall submit a Monthly Vehicle Inventory Report to the COR on the 15th of 
each month. This information should be organized in an Excel file format according to the 
structure described in S4 Part A in Section 4 and submitted to the COR each month 
until all vehicles have been discarded. 
 
B. 
INVOICING REPORT 
 
The “Invoicing Report” allows NHTSA to identify and reconcile its internal invoicing 
records against the Contractor’s. This information should be organized in an Excel file 
format according to the structure outlined under S4 Part B in Section 4 and submitted to 
the COR each month. A working template will be provided by the COR. 
 
C. 
ATD AND SENSOR INVENTORY STATUS REPORT 
 
An “ATD and Sensor Inventory Report”, in Excel file format and according to the structure 
outlined under S4 Part C in Section 4 shall be submitted to the COR each month. 
 
1.2 
LABORATORY NOTICE OF TEST FAILURE REPORT 
 
An apparent test failure, as described by Section 13.1, A of the main test procedure shall be 
communicated by telephone to the COR within 24 hours with written notification emailed within 48 
hours (Saturdays and Sundays excluded).  A Laboratory Notice of Test Failure (see S3 in Section 
4) with a copy of the related NCAP test data sheet(s) and preliminary data plot(s) shall be 
included.   
 
 
In the event of a test failure, a post-test calibration check of some of the critically sensitive test 
equipment and instrumentation may be required for verification of accuracy.  The necessity of 
calibration shall be at the COR’s discretion and shall be performed without additional costs to the 
Office of Crashworthiness Standards (OCWS). 
 
1.3 
SIDE NCAP POLE TEST DELIVERABLES 
 
Required deliverables for each test are discussed in this section.  A Schedule of Deliverables is 
also provided at the end of this section.  
 
A. 
REPORT OF VEHICLE CONDITION 
 
The pre-test section of the Report of Vehicle Condition (see S2 in Section 4) should be 
completed upon delivery and emailed to the OCWS within 48 working hours. In addition 
to the report, the contractor should include a copy of the Monroney label received with 
the vehicle. 
 
B. 
FTP WEBSITE 
 
 
To expedite data transfer between the Contractor and NHTSA, a File Transfer Protocol 
(FTP) website will be made available to Contractors through an FTP coordinator. 
 
 
(1) 
ACCESSING THE FTP SITE 
 
The Point of Contact at each test facility will receive an e-mail with the FTP site 
address and a unique username and password to access the website.  A new 


## Page 154

3 
Rev. 03/03/2020 
 
password will be issued on the 1st of each month.  Any FTP client can be used to 
access and upload data. 
 
 
(2)  
UPLOADING TEST DATA 
 
 
 
Associated test documentation (test data, photos, videos, reports, etc.) required 
for each relevant deliverable must be placed in organized and labeled folders such 
that each folder’s contents are easily recognizable.  Once the data is organized, 
the Contractor shall place all folders into ONE (1) .zip file per test via the FTP 
website.  The .zip file should then be uploaded using an FTP client. 
 
To ensure successful transfers, please contact your network administrator and 
confirm that FTP transfers are permitted.  Set your FTP client program to upload 
in passive (PASV) mode and set the “file exists” action to “skip”.  For FTP 
assistance, please contact the COR. 
 
NOTE:   If the Contractor is experiencing difficulty uploading the test data to the FTP site, 
it is the Contractor’s responsibility to alert NHTSA in order to arrange for them to 
download the data instead. 
 
C.  
QUICKLOOK REPORT 
 
The Quicklook Report is a preliminary summary of the test that shall be e-mailed to the 
OCWS within 24 hours of the impact event.  The Report should detail all relevant injury 
criteria, vehicle information, air bag deployment, and evidence of Indicant FMVSS No. 
214P, FMVSS No. 301, and Indicant FMVSS No. 305 (if applicable) compliance, and 
should include data traces relevant to the injury criteria it contains.  Also, anything of 
interest or out of the ordinary should be included in the Quicklook Report in the comments 
section. 
 
NOTE: The Quicklook Report, including the relevant data traces, should be supplied to any 
vehicle manufacturer representatives present at the conclusion of an NCAP crash 
test. However, no other information should be provided at that time without explicit 
permission from the COR.  
 
D. 
DATA TAPE 
 
Within three (3) working days of the test, the Contractor shall e-mail NHTSA the test 
data (data tape) as a .zip file, formatted using NHTSA’s software and test data formatting 
guidelines.   
             
Data entry software (ENTRÉE) may also be downloaded from the website and used to 
generate the specification data files as defined in the guides.  Visit 
https://www.nhtsa.gov/databases-and-software/entree-windows. The latest revision to 
Volume I: Vehicle Test should be used and can be found at 
https://one.nhtsa.gov/Research/Databases-and-Software/NHTSA-Test-Reference-
Guides. 
 
 Any questions pertaining to this software should be directed to NCAP COR or to the 
following technical support department: 
 
U.S. Dept. of Transportation 
NHTSA/NVS-300 
W46-318 
1200 New Jersey Ave SE 
Washington, DC 20590 
 


## Page 155

4 
Rev. 03/03/2020 
 
 
E. 
QUALITY CONTROL PACKAGE 
 
The Quality Control Package is a .zip file that includes all of the information necessary for 
quality control review.  It serves as a summary of the test and includes, organized by 
folders labeled appropriately:  
 
 
The test data (data tape)  
o 
Per section 1.3, D of this appendix 
 
Photographs 
o 
Labeled in order per Section 2.5 of this appendix 
o 
“Impact for Web” photo – 710 x 410 pixels, landscape orientation 
 
Videos 
o 
High-speed videos per Section 9.1 of the main side impact rigid pole test 
procedure, labeled appropriately 
o 
Real-time videos per Section 9.1 of the main side impact rigid pole test 
procedure, labeled appropriately 
o 
Documentation video per Section 9.8 of the main side impact rigid pole 
test procedure, labeled appropriately 
 
Pre- and post-test dummy qualification data 
o 
Per guidelines in the appropriate appendix 
 
Report of Vehicle Condition  
o 
The entirety of S2 – Report of Vehicle Condition, found in Section 4 of 
this appendix 
 
Quicklook Report previously e-mailed to the OCWS 
o 
Per section 1.3, C of this appendix 
 
CMM seating worksheet Excel file 
 
The Quality Control Package shall be uploaded to the FTP site within five (5) 
business days of the test for review by the OCWS.  Providing this data in a timely 
manner will ensure that the Contractor and the COR will be able to discuss the details of 
both test conduct and report content soon after the test is conducted. 
 
The Contractor will also provide website-related material with this data.  The Contractor 
shall provide a .jpg image of the vehicle impact appropriate for use on the website. This 
photo should be a duplicate of photo number 70 in the Side NCAP Pole photo list found in 
section 2.5 of this appendix. The photo should be labeled as follows: 
 
<Model Year><Make><Model>SideNCAPPoleImpactforWeb.jpg 
 
It shall be 710 pixels wide by 410 pixels tall, landscape (horizontal) orientation, and of a 
high image quality.   
 
Camera No. 1, the Real-Time Pan View of Impact Camera as described in Section 9.1 of 
the main side NCAP rigid pole test procedure, should be provided in .wmv format (unless 
otherwise specified by NHTSA personnel) so it may serve as a web-ready video of the 
impact event. This movie file shall be approximately 300-400 kb in size and shall be labeled 
as follows: 
 
<Model Year><Make><Model><Number of 
Doors><Body>SideNCAPPoleImpactforWeb.wmv 
 
The Report of Vehicle Condition (see S2 in Section 4) shall be completed by the Contractor 
and submitted to the COR as part of the QCPackage.zip file. The first page of the report 
shall be completed when the test vehicle arrives at the testing laboratory. The second page 
of the report is completed after the test. The sheets shall be legible (hand written sheets 
are unacceptable) and complete (all information requested is filled out).   


## Page 156

5 
Rev. 03/03/2020 
 
  
F. 
PRELIMINARY (DRAFT) TEST REPORT 
 
Contractors are required to submit, via e-mail to the OCWS, the draft version of the Final 
Test Report (.pdf or .doc), within two (2) calendar weeks of the test.  If the electronic 
file is larger than 20 MB, it is requested that the Contractor upload the file to the FTP site 
instead. 
 
The filename for the Preliminary Draft Test Report should be formatted as follows: 
 
<NHTSANO><Model Year><Make & Model><Body>SideNCAPPoleDraftReport.pdf  
 
See Section 2 of this appendix for content requirements for the Preliminary and Final Test 
Reports. The Contractor should use detailed descriptions of all test events.  Any events 
that are associated with the pass/fail of FMVSS No. 214 or FMVSS No. 301, FMVSS No. 
305, or that are of technical interest, shall also be included.   
 
Contractors are required to review and proofread all test reports before submittal to the 
COR.  The OCWS will not act as a report quality control office for Contractors.  Reports 
containing a significant number of errors will be returned to the Contractor for correction 
and a hold will be placed on invoice payment for the particular test.  The OCWS will alert 
the Contractor to minimal corrections that should be made prior to submission of the Final 
Test Report. 
 
G. 
FINAL TEST REPORT AND DELIVERABLES 
 
The Final Test Report and associated documentation, including test data, properly 
labeled and numbered photographs and videos (including documentation, high-speed, 
and real-time, and those for the web), are relied upon as the chronicle of the NCAP test.  
Each Final Test Report must be a complete document capable of standing by itself.  The 
Contractor should use detailed descriptions of all test events.  Any events that are not 
directly associated with the side NCAP pole test, but that are of technical interest, should 
also be included.  The Contractor should include as much detail as possible in the report.   
 
The Final Test Report and associated deliverables will be released to the public domain 
after review and acceptance by the COR.  For these reasons, all deliverables must be 
complete and error-free.  Final Test Reports containing errors will be returned to the 
Contractor for correction and a hold will be placed on invoice payment for the particular 
test. 
 
Note: Only those photos required in the Final Test Report, as set forth in this procedure, 
shall be included unless the OCWS requests the inclusion of additional photos to 
document specific test events or anomalies.   
 
The Contractor shall upload the Final Test Report and final versions of the associated 
test data, photos, and videos as a .zip file to the FTP website within two (2) weeks of 
receiving data tape and Draft Test Report corrections from the OCWS.  
 
The format for its filename should be as follows: 
  
<NHTSANO><Model Year><Make & Model><Body>SideNCAPPoleFinalDeliverables.zip 
 
H. 
VEHICLE AIR BAG AND RESTRAINT DEACTIVATION REPORT 
 
A “Vehicle Air Bag and Restraint Deactivation and Removal Report” (see S6 in Section 
4) should be completed and submitted to the COR within 14 days of receiving 
authorization to complete restraint deactivation activities.

Block No. 16—ABSTRACT 
 
A 32.20 km/h, 75 oblique impact Side NCAP Test was conducted on the 
subject 20XX SaferRider 4-door Sedan in accordance with the 
specifications of the Office of Crashworthiness Standards Side NCAP Pole 
Laboratory Test Procedure for the generation of consumer information on 
vehicle side pole crash protection.  The test was conducted at the ABC 
Laboratories facility in Detroit, Michigan, on November 15, 20XX. 
 
The impact velocity was 31.9 km/h, and the ambient temperature at the 
struck (driver’s) side of the target vehicle at the time of impact was 28°C.  
The test vehicle post-test maximum crush was 250 mm at level 3.  The 
test vehicle’s performance was as follows: 
 
 
Driver ATD (SID-IIs)

The two doors on the struck side of the vehicle did not separate from the 
body at the hinges or latches and the opposite doors did not open during 
the side impact event.

2.3 
SECTION 1 – PURPOSE AND SUMMARY OF TEST 
 
PURPOSE 
 
This section briefly describes the purpose for conducting the side impact test and states the 
appropriate test procedure followed during the test.  The following language is provided as an 
example: 
 
This side pole impact test is part of the MY     New Car Assessment Program Side Impact Test 
Program, sponsored by the National Highway Traffic Safety Administration (NHTSA), under 
contract number                      . The purpose of this test is to generate comparative side impact 
performance in a 20XX SaferRider 4-door Sedan. The side impact test was conducted in 
accordance with the Office of Crashworthiness Standard’s Side NCAP Pole Laboratory Test 
Procedure, dated                      .  
 
SUMMARY  
 
This section gives a summary of the side impact event. The following is an example of the 
content needed in this section: 
 
A rigid pole side impact test was conducted on a 20XX SaferRider 4-door Sedan.  The subject 
vehicle was towed into the rigid pole at an angle of 75o and a velocity of 31.90 km/h. The test was 
conducted by the ABC Laboratories in Detroit, Michigan, on Month Day, 20XX.  Pre-test and post-
test photographs of the test vehicle and side impact dummy (SID-IIs) are included in this report. 
 
One Part 572V (SID-IIs) dummy was placed in the driver designated seating position according to 
instructions specified in the OCWS Side NCAP Pole Laboratory Test Procedure, dated 
___________.  The side impact event was documented by ___ cameras.  Camera locations and 
other pertinent camera information are included in this report. 
 
The Part 572V (SID-IIs) Dummy was instrumented accordingly: 
 
Primary and Redundant Head CG Triaxial Accelerometers 
Head Triaxial Angular Rate Sensors 
Thorax Upper, Middle, and Lower Rib Displacement Potentiometers 
Abdomen Upper and Lower Rib Displacement Potentiometers 
Lower Spine (T12) Triaxial Accelerometers 
Iliac Load Cell 
Acetabulum Load Cell

GENERAL COMMENTS 
 
EXAMPLE:  The driver door became unlatched and opened during impact. The width of the 
opening at the latch was 6.5 inches.  The fuel line was broken upon impact and fuel leaked at a 
rate of 30 oz. per minute.  The side curtain airbag failed to deploy. The driver’s side torso air bag 
deployed late, and thus failed to provide adequate protection to the occupant.  The HIC values for 
the driver exceeded the threshold. 
 
2.4 
SECTION 2 – OCCUPANT AND VEHICLE INFORMATION/DATA SHEETS 
 
This section requires the reporting of all information found in the following data sheets.  Data sheets 
can be found in Section 3 of these Deliverable Guidelines.  The Contractor may expand upon the 
data sheets if desired; however, the data must be presented in the order listed under the above 
“SAMPLE TEST REPORT LAYOUT”. Any additional inclusions MUST be placed after the required 
sheets. 
 
2.5 
APPENDIX A – PHOTOGRAPHIC DOCUMENTATION 
 
The following photographs shall be included as Appendix A of the Final Test Report, two photos 
per page and approximately 4 inches by 6 inches in size, at a minimum. Vehicle information 
placards for the test vehicle identifying the vehicle, barrier, test date, and NHTSA number, along 
with an indication of whether the photo was taken pre-test or post-test, shall appear in each 
photograph and be legible. In cases where it may be unreasonable to include this long-form 
placard, an indication of NHTSA number only will suffice. A time/date stamp on each photo is also 
highly recommended. 


## Page 165

14 
Rev. 03/03/2020 
 
 
The following photographs should be included with the Quality Control Package and labeled as 
indicated.  The text in parenthesis is for clarification purposes only and need not be included.  If 
additional photographs are needed to satisfy the requirements of report Appendix A, including but 
not limited to, photograph required for indicant FMVSS No. 305 testing, subsequent photos 
should be lettered and labeled appropriately. 
 
Additional photographs which further describe what is visible in Photograph Nos. 1 – 104, and if 
applicable, 305-1 – 305-38, should be labeled with the most relevant photograph number followed 
by a, b, c, etc. For example, if the laboratory would like to provide more than one photograph of 
the pre-test ballast view, the photographs should be labeled as follows: 
 
062 – Pre-Test Ballast View (required photo) 
062a – Pre-Test Ballast View (additional view) 
 
Any additional photographs taken for documentation of vehicle anomalies, safety concerns, test 
details, etc. which do not fit under the photograph descriptions below should be appropriately 
labeled and shall follow the list of preceding required photographs in numerical order. 
 
All pre-test photographs should be taken immediately prior to impact (i.e., within the hour 
preceding impact after the manufacturer has been given an opportunity to review the test 
set-up) and all post-test photographs should be taken immediately following impact 
(within the hour following impact before the manufacturer has been given the opportunity 
to examine the crashed vehicle.

of the certification data provided by the supplier.

Appendix E of the test report should include the seating procedure worksheets included in the 
seating procedure Excel file (to be provided by NHTSA). Furthermore, the digital measurements 
taken for the seating procedure worksheet should be used to create two-dimensional plots (XY, 
XZ, and YZ) of the dummies. These plots must be included in Appendix E.  
3. 
DATA SHEETS 
 
Data sheets are provided as tools to document test data in the test report format outlined in 
Section 2 of this appendix.  The Contractor is not restricted from using other data sheets or 
expanding the data sheets provided herein.  Nevertheless, for consistency and uniformity in 
reporting data, the Contractor must present the data in the order outlined in this section.

SEAT BACK ANGLE ADJUSTMENT 
The driver’s seat back is positioned such that the dummy’s  
head is level.  The front center and front passenger’s seat backs  
are positioned in a similar manner as the driver’s seat back.  The  
struck-side rear passenger seat back is positioned in accordance  
with the information provided by the manufacturer on S1 – Vehicle  
Setup Information for the 5th percentile female dummy in a Side NCAP  
MDB test.  The rear center and non-struck side rear passenger’s seat  
back is set to match the struck-side rear seat back.

4. 
SUPPLEMENTAL VEHICLE AND TESTING REPORTS 
 
Supplemental Vehicle and Testing Reports, like Data Sheets, are provided as tools to use in the exchange 
of data between the COTR and the Contractor.  However, these reports are not part of the Final Test 
Report.  The Contractor is not restricted from using other tools or expanding the reports outlined in this 
section. 
 
A. 
S1 – Vehicle Setup Information 
 
A “Vehicle Setup Information” report will be supplied by the COR to the Contractor before 
testing preparation.  Information on this report is supplied by the automobile manufacturer 
to aid in the initial test setup and shall be considered as reference material.  After vehicle 
preparation is complete, the Vehicle Setup Information report shall be retained by the 
Contractor for at least 5 years. 
 
B. 
S2 – Report of Vehicle Condition 
 
See section 1.3, A for further information regarding the Report of Vehicle Condition form. 
 
C. 
S3 - Laboratory Notice of Invalid Test or Apparent Test Failure 
 
See Section 13.1 of the main Side Impact NCAP Rigid Pole Test Procedure for further 
information regarding the Laboratory Notice of Invalid Test or Apparent Test Failure report. 
 
D. 
S4 – Monthly Status Reports 
 
See Section 1.1 for further information regarding the following monthly status reports: 
 
(1) 
Part A - Vehicle Inventory Report 
 
(2) 
Part B -  Invoicing Report  
 
(3) 
Part C -  ATD and Sensor Inventory Report 
 
E. 
S5 - Quicklook Report 
 
See Section 1.3, C for further information on the Quicklook Report. 
 
F. 
S6 – Vehicle Air Bag and Restraint Deactivation and Removal Report 
 
See Section 7.3 of the main Side Impact NCAP Rigid Pole Test Procedure for information 
on the Vehicle Air Bag and Restraint Deactivation and Removal Report.

Rev. 03/03/2020

14. 
LOCATION OF CARGO-CARRYING AREA AND LIST OF REMOVABLE PARTS 
 
On occasion, NCAP needs to add ballast weight to vehicles in order to achieve target 
test weight.  If a traditional cargo-carrying area like a trunk, rear hatch area, or truck bed 
is not present on this vehicle, please describe the nature and location of the vehicle’s 
intended cargo-carrying area below. 
______________________________________________________________________
______________________________________________________________________ 
 
NCAP will also remove the following parts to reduce vehicle weight if the target test 
weight cannot be achieved: 
 
Frontal NCAP test:  spare tire, rear door windows, rear radio speakers, interior door 
trim on the rear doors, rear seat cushions, outboard mirrors, taillights, rear bumper 
 
Side NCAP test:  spare tire, rear radio speakers, interior door trim and windows on 
non-struck side, outboard mirrors on non-struck side, taillights, rear bumper 
 
Please prioritize the items in this list in order of removal preference for each NCAP 
test.  Please make a note of any parts that should not be removed because they serve 
as load bearing or structural components and therefore, will likely affect NCAP test 
performance.  Also, please feel free to add additional items which are not listed if their 
removal is deemed acceptable.

S4 Part A - VEHICLE INVENTORY REPORT 
 
Each month, the Contractor should provide the COR with a report of the NCAP-related vehicles they have in 
inventory. This should include NCAP-owned, optional, and lab-owned retest vehicles. If the Contractor is in 
possession of vehicles that are associated with more than one NCAP contract, each tab in the file should only 
include details related to one contract number. Each tab should be named using the contract number along with 
an indication of the test direction (e.g., front or side). The chart below should be recreated in an Excel file with 
data added according to the chart key below. 
 
The Excel file name should be structured as follows: 
 
< 3 Letter Lab Name/TSTPRF><Year><Month>Form 4a Vehicle Inventory Report.xlsx 
 
All columns shown below must be included, in the same order shown. Additional columns of pertinent information 
may be added to (but not inserted in between) these columns. 
 
No. 
Test

to? 
1 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
2 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Chart Key: 
 
 
No.: Sequential number identifying each vehicle purchased under the contract. 
 
Test Mode: Indicate the type of crash test performed on the vehicle: frontal, side MDB, or side pole 
 
Year/Make/Model: Indicate the year, make, and model of the vehicle 
 
NHTSA No.: Indicate the vehicle’s NHTSA number 
 
Owner: Indicate the owner of the NCAP vehicle 
 
VIN: Indicate the vehicle’s 17-digit identification number (VIN) 
 
Delivery Date: Indicate the date the vehicle was received at your laboratory 
 
Crash Test Date: Indicate the date the vehicle was subject to crash testing. 
 
Final Odometer: Indicate the final odometer reading just prior to releasing or transferring the vehicle out 
of your possession 
 
Restraints Deactivated?: Indicate “no” in this field until instructions are received from the COR to 
deactivate all of the vehicle restraints. After those activities are completed, indicate “yes.” 
 
Vehicle Disposal Date: Indicate the date the vehicle is transferred out of your possession. 
 
Transferred to?: Indicate the recipient of the vehicle once is it transferred out of your possession.

S4 Part B - INVOICING REPORT 
 
Each month, the Contractor should supply the COR with a report of current invoicing activities.  
 
The Excel file name should be structured as follows: 
 
< 3 Letter Lab Name/TSTPRF><Year><Month>Form 4b Invoicing Report.xlsx 
 
If the Contractor is invoicing items on multiple NCAP contracts, each tab in the Excel file should only include details related to one contract 
number. Each tab should be named using the contract number along with an indication of the test direction (e.g., front or side). 
 
The header and chart information detailed below should be replicated for each separate delivery order issued under the contract, so that all 
delivery orders issued under a contract are contained on one tab in the Excel file. The lab should construct a completely new chart for each 
delivery order issued under a contract based on the items included in each subsequent delivery order. 
 
All header items and chart columns shown below must be included, in the same order shown. Additional chart columns of pertinent information 
may be added to (but not inserted in between) these chart columns. For ease of discussion, the “left” and “right” sides of the chart are discussed 
separately. Spreadsheets should be designed according to the header, “left,” and “right” chart keys below. 
 
In addition to building in the calculations and functionality described throughout the following sections, the Contractor should use conditional 
formatting or other functions in Excel to flag or highlight information that could lead to problems such as invoicing more contract line item numbers 
(CLINs) than were ordered or charging the incorrect price. 
 
Header Key: 
 
Contract No: DTNH221XD00XXX 
 
Delivery Order:

$5,000.00

$800.00
 
 
Contract No: Place the contract number in a larger font at the top left corner of the sheet. This should be duplicated towards the top left 
corner of each delivery order chart generated on the tab. 
 
Delivery Order: Delivery order number. 
 
Requisition No: Requisition number. 
 
DO PoP Start Date: The start date for the delivery order’s period of performance (PoP). 
 
DO PoP End Date: The end date for the delivery order’s period of performance (PoP). 
 
PoP Extension End Date: The new period of performance end date (PoP) if the delivery order end date has been extended. 
 
Total Award: The total funds awarded on the delivery order. 
 
Invoiced: Subtotal of items invoiced on the delivery order thus far. This field should contain a function to calculate the sum of the Line

Rev. 03/03/2020

Total column described under “Left” Chart Key below. 
 
Balance: The remaining funds on the delivery order. This field should contain a function to calculate the difference between Total Award 
and Invoiced.

the Total fields from the “Right Side” of the spreadsheet.

 “Right Side” of Chart 
 
The columns on the “right side” of the spreadsheet are more dynamic than the “left side” columns. For each new delivery order, a different set of 
contract line item numbers (CLINs) will be included. For each CLIN contained on a delivery order, a block of specific information should be placed 
to the right of the information described in the “Left Side” section above. The number of these blocks depends on the variety of CLINs included on 
a delivery order. In turn, this dictates how many columns will need to be summed to propagate the Line Total field described in the “Left Side” 
section.



difference between the sum of the items in the Qty column and the Qty Ordered cell. 


 
Total: This field should contain a function to calculate the total cost under the subject CLIN charged for the Test Item, using the related Qty 
and Unit Price fields. All Total cells on a given line should sum to inform the Line Total cell for that Test Item. 
 
Count: This field should be used to track the quantity of this CLIN used versus the Qty Ordered as reported on the invoice.

S4 Part C - ATD and SENSOR INVENTORY REPORT 
 
Each month, the Contractor should supply the COR with a summary of the NHTSA NCAP GFP they have in-
house other than test vehicles. This shall include ATDs, sensors, and any other equipment that has been 
provided by NCAP. 
 
The Excel file name should be structured as follows: 
< 3 Letter Lab Name/TSTPRF><Year><Month>Form 4c ATD and Sensor Report.xlsx 
 
Each Excel file should contain at least three tabs. The following sections discuss the structure and content of 
each tab. The Contractor may include additional information in this monthly submission, but additional information 
should be included on subsequent tabs in the spreadsheet.

dummies and related equipment (such as head forms and leg forms) that the Contractor has in-house:

APPENDIX D 
SID-IIs HEAD ANGULAR RATE SENSOR 
POLARITY CHECK PROCEDURE
 


## Page 234

D1 
APPENDIX D - SID-IIs HEADANGULAR RATE SENSOR (ARS) POLARITY 
CHECK PROCEDURE 
 
Purpose: 
 
This Appendix provides a practical methodology for checking and documenting the 
polarity of the data channel for each dummy mounted head angular rate sensor (ARS) 
relative to the NHTSA sign convention. Documenting the polarity of channels prior to 
testing serves to increase the confidence that they will record data correctly during an 
event. The polarities in this document are the same as those of the SAE J211. 
 
SAE J211 Procedure: 
 
The body coordinate system used for reference is attached to the dummy and is x positive 
pointing forward, y positive pointing to the right, and z positive pointing down. 
 
To check the polarity of the head ARS, the head and chest must be moved in opposite 
directions to induce a measurable rotational rate. Moving the right ear toward the right 
shoulder should result in a positive ωx. Moving the chin away from the sternum results in 
a positive ωy and moving the chin towards the right shoulder will have a positive ωz. If 
any of these motions do not result in a positive reading, the polarity needs to be changed 
to agree with the sign convention. A sign change in the software may be the simplest 
solution. 
 
Polarity Check Data Sheet for Head Angular Rate Sensors 
Dummy Type:  
Serial No.  
Date: 
Direction Motion 
Polarity 
ωx 
Rotate right ear toward right shoulder 
+ (positive) 
ωy 
Rotate chin away from sternum 
+ (positive) 
ωz 
Rotate chin toward right shoulder 
+ (positive)

## Page 237

Side NCAP Pole - E2 
1. PURPOSE AND APPLICATION 
The New Car Assessment Program’s (NCAP’s) side impact rigid pole test procedure is 
based on a related safety standard, Federal Motor Vehicle Safety Standard (FMVSS) No. 
214, which specifies performance requirements for the protection of vehicle occupants in 
crashes. The assessment of certain FMVSS-related parameters during NCAP testing 
allows the Office of Crashworthiness Standards (OCWS) to gain supplemental 
information on the test vehicle. 
 
NOTE: All variables are to be evaluated at NCAP’s 20mph (32.20km/h) side 
impact pole test vehicle velocity.  
 
This document is an appendix to the main side impact pole laboratory test procedure 
provided by the National Highway Traffic Safety Administration (NHTSA), Office of 
Crashworthiness Standards (OCWS) for the purpose of presenting guidelines for a 
uniform testing data and information recording format, and providing suggestions for the 
use of specific equipment and procedures for contracted testing laboratories. The data 
correspond to requirements for indicant testing in accords with FMVSS No. 301 and 305. 
The OCWS test procedure is not intended to limit or restrain a contractor from 
developing or utilizing any testing techniques or equipment that will assist in procuring 
the required test data. However, applicability of any such testing technique or equipment 
is subject to prior approval by the COR. 
 
The indicant test procedures presented in this appendix are applicable to vehicles tested 
under the main side impact pole NCAP test procedure. It is the contractor’s responsibility 
to follow the most updated versions of all related test procedures when conducting these 
assessments as part of side impact pole NCAP testing. These vehicles must also meet the 
requirements set forth in this Appendix.  
 
Vehicles will be tested to the requirements contained herein in conjunction with the 
dynamic requirements for side impact pole NCAP tests. The test facility must be able to 
conduct these NCAP tests. The facility must meet the minimum requirements regarding 
weighing capability, speed measurement systems, test surface, tow-road, abort system, 
barriers, and all other requirements. 
 
2. DEFINITIONS 
See main SINCAP Pole Procedure, Section 10 for additional Definitions. 
 
DAYLIGHT OPENING (DLO)  
Maximum unobstructed opening through the glazing surface (windshield), including 
reveal or garnish moldings adjoining the surface, as measured parallel to the outer surface 
of the glazing material. 
 
ELECTROLYTE SPILLAGE 
The fall, flow, or run of propulsion battery electrolyte in, on, or from the vehicle, 
including wetness resulting from capillary action. 


## Page 238

Side NCAP Pole - E3 
 
FORWARD CONTROL VEHICLE (FCV)  
Configuration in which more than half of the engine length is rearward of the foremost 
point of the windshield base and the steering wheel hub is in the forward quarter of the 
vehicle length. 
 
PROPULSION BATTERY SYSTEM COMPONENT 
Any part of a propulsion battery module, interconnect, venting system, battery restraint 
device, and battery box or container that holds the individual battery modules used for 
propulsion. 
 
3. PRE-TEST REQUIREMENTS  
3.1. 
DETAILED TEST AND QUALITY CONTROL PROCEDURES REQUIRED 
 
Prior to conducting the indicant test, if requested by the COR, the Contractor may be 
required to submit a detailed in-house test procedure (to the COR) that includes: 
 
a. A step-by-step description of the methodology to be used. 
b. A written Quality Control (QC) Procedure which shall include calibrations, the data 
review process, report review, and the people assigned to perform QC on each task. 
c. A complete listing of test equipment with instrument accuracy and calibration dates. 
d. Detailed check off lists to be used during the test and during data review. These lists 
shall include all test procedure requirements and any additional requirements 
pertaining to the applicable safety standard for which testing is being performed. 
Each separate check off sheet shall identify the laboratory, test date, vehicle, and test 
technicians. These check sheets shall be used to document that all requirements and 
procedures have been complied with. If requested, these sheets shall be submitted 
with the test report. 
e. There shall be no contradiction between the OCWS Laboratory Test Procedure and 
the Contractor's in-house test procedure. 
 
4. FMVSS No. 301 INDICANT TEST 
4.1. 
GENERAL REQUIREMENTS 
This indicant test is based on FMVSS No. 301, which specifies performance requirements 
for the integrity of motor vehicle fuel systems. It is the contractor’s responsibility to follow 
the most updated test procedure when conducting this assessment as part of NCAP testing. 
 
1. 
SIDE RIGID POLE IMPACT 
When a vehicle is subject to a side impact pole NCAP test, the following fuel leakage 
conditions must be met: 
 
 
 


## Page 239

Side NCAP Pole - E4 
TIME 
MAX. FLUID SPILLAGE 
From impact until vehicle motion ceases 
1 ounce by weight 
For 5 minute period after vehicle motion ceases 
5 ounces by weight 
For the next 25 minutes 
1 ounce by weight/minute 
 
2. 
STATIC ROLLOVER 
After a vehicle is subject to a side impact pole NCAP test and placed on a static 
rollover machine, the following fuel leakage conditions must be met: 
 
TIME 
MAX. FLUID SPILLAGE 
For 5 minute period from onset of rotation at each 
90° position 
5 ounces by weight 
For 6th minute  
1 ounce by weight 
For 7th minute (if required) 
1 ounce by weight 
For 8th minute (if required) 
1 ounce by weight 
 
4.2. 
FACILITY AND EQUIPMENT – PRE-TEST REQUIREMENTS) 
1. 
STATIC ROLLOVER MACHINE 
The Contractor must have a rollover machine capable of rotating the barrier-
impacted test vehicle about its longitudinal axis with the axis kept horizontal, to 
each successive increment of 90°, 180°, and 270° at a uniform rate, with 90° of 
rotation taking place in any time interval from 1 to 3 minutes.  
 
 
2. 
STODDARD COLLECTION CONTAINERS AND STOPWATCH 
Containers for the collection of Stoddard solvent and a calibrated stopwatch for 
timing the fluid collection intervals are required. Leakage will be collected for the 5 
minute period from the beginning of rotation plus any additional 1 minute 
collection periods that are required. Containers must be labeled before they are 
photographed. 
 
3. 
OTHER TEST INSTRUMENTATION 
The Contractor shall provide the necessary equipment to permanently record and 
display data. The data shall be included in the final test report and on the electronic 
data media. 
 
4.3. 
FUEL SYSTEM INTEGRITY PROCEDURE 
After the vehicle impact, fuel system Stoddard solvent leakage (if any) should be 
collected by hand and documented with a real-time (24-30 fps) video camera and 
stopwatch. The “tea cup method” involves simply placing a collection vessel beneath the 
leakage source and timing the intervals of several collected volumes. The collected 


## Page 240

Side NCAP Pole - E5 
Stoddard solvent samples can subsequently be measured and spillage rates calculated. If 
the “tea cup method” is used, the test personnel must be in position to reach observation 
points around the test vehicle at the instant the vehicle comes to rest after the impact 
event. 
 
 
NOTE: It is the Contractor’s responsibility to collect any suspect liquids 
leaking from the vehicle post-test and analyze the contents if 
necessary. 
 
 
4.4. 
STATIC ROLLOVER PROCEDURE 
The Contractor must conduct a static rollover test within 30 minutes after the vehicle 
impact. The Contractor must keep the test vehicle under constant observation for 
Stoddard solvent leakage during the transition between impact and static rollover testing. 
 
When the test vehicle is rotated in a fixture on its longitudinal axis to each successive 
increment of 90°, following an impact crash, Stoddard solvent spillage, from the onset of 
rotational motion, shall not exceed a total of 5 ounces by weight for the first 5 minutes of 
testing at each successive 90° increment. For the remaining testing period, at each 
increment of 90°, solvent spillage during any l-minute interval shall not exceed 1ounce 
by weight. 
 
4.5. 
STATIC ROLLOVER TEST CONDITIONS 
Prior to conducting any static rollover test, ATDs should be removed from the vehicle. 
Within 30 minutes of vehicle impact, the Contractor should place the vehicle in the test 
fixture, where it may be rotated in a test fixture about its longitudinal axis, with the axis 
kept horizontal, to each successive increment of the following: 
 
Rotation 1 - 90° 
Rotation 2 - 180° 
Rotation 3 - 270° 
Rotation 4 - 360° 
 
Rotation 1 must be done such that the vehicle’s fuel filler cap or plug is on the bottom of 
the vehicle when the rotation is completed. Rotation must take place at a uniform rate, 
with 90° of rotation taking place in any time interval from 1 to 3 minutes. After reaching 
each 90° increment, the vehicle is held in that position for 5 minutes. 
 
Leakage will be collected for the 5-minute period from the beginning of rotation plus up 
to three 1-minute collection periods. Containers for the collection of possible Stoddard 
solvent spillage and a calibrated stopwatch for timing the fluid collection intervals are 
required. Containers must be labeled before they are photographed. 
 
The Contractor should complete Data Sheet No. 12 in Appendix C of the main side 
impact pole NCAP test procedure and include it with the test report. 
 


## Page 241

Side NCAP Pole - E6 
5.  FMVSS No. 305 INDICANT TEST 
5.1. 
GENERAL REQUIREMENTS 
This indicant test is based on FMVSS No. 305, which specifies performance 
requirements for the limitation of electrolyte spillage, retention of propulsion batteries, 
and electrical isolation of the chassis from the high-voltage system during the crash 
event. It applies to vehicles that use electricity as propulsion power. 
 
It is the contractor’s responsibility to follow the most updated test procedure when 
conducting this assessment as part of NCAP testing. 
 
When a vehicle is subject to a side impact pole NCAP test, it shall NOT: 
a. Spill more than 5.0 liters of electrolyte from propulsion batteries outside the 
passenger compartment, and no visible trace of electrolyte shall spill into the 
passenger compartment. Spillage is measured from the time the vehicle ceases 
motion after a barrier impact test until 30 minutes thereafter, and throughout any 
static rollover after a barrier impact test.  
b. Have any propulsion battery system component located inside the passenger 
compartment move from the location in which they are installed. 
c. Have any propulsion battery system component located outside the passenger 
compartment enter the passenger compartment. 
d. Fail to maintain an electrical isolation of no less than 500 ohms/volt between the 
propulsion battery system and the vehicle’s electricity-conducting structure. 
 
5.2. 
FACILITY AND EQUIPMENT: PRE-TEST REQUIREMENTS 
1. 
VOLTAGE MEASUREMENT DEVICE AND INTERFACE 
The voltmeter used in this test shall measure AC and DC values and have an 
internal impedance of at least 10MΩ. 
 
Voltage measurements throughout this test must be made quickly and safely. To 
ensure these requirements are met, the testing lab must devise, for COR approval, a 
test interface port or other device to facilitate these voltage measurements. All 
voltage measurements shall be immediate upon connection to the interface port. 
This test interface port equipment shall be easily accessible from the exterior of the 
vehicle and connected to the appropriate propulsion system and battery components 
via laboratory installed wires. The external mounting of this test interface port shall 
be configured such that no movement, interference, or damage will result to it from 
a barrier crash test. The test interface port shall incorporate a fusible link and any 
other necessary safety device or usage procedure to protect the data measurement 
and recording equipment from damage, and the test technicians from electrical 
shock. 
 
A terminal block or circuit board is recommended as a means to providing an 
external interface  
 


## Page 242

Side NCAP Pole - E7 
The following is an example quoted from Transport Canada document, “Test 
Procedures, Frontal Impact 208-212-301F-305F, No. 03-002” 
 
“This kit is composed of a PVC box compliant with the electrical code and 
containing insulated banana connectors that allow the measuring equipment to 
be connected for the verification of the standard. A warning light indicates the 
presence of voltage inside the box. A shielded cable with three conductors, 20 
feet in length and capable of supporting 600 volts, connects the box to the 
vehicle’s electrical system. This cable is covered with orange-colored 
mechanical protection (similar to the Hybrid vehicle high-voltage 
identification code). The box is protected by a 0.5-amp fuse. 
 
2. 
STATIC ROLLOVER MACHINE 
The rollover machine must be capable of rotating, and holding in place, the 
impacted NCAP test vehicle up to 5443 kg about its longitudinal axis with the axis 
kept horizontal, to each successive increment of 90°, 180°, and 270° at a uniform 
rate, with 90° of rotation taking place in any time interval from 1 to 3 minutes. 
Leakage will be collected for the 5-minute period from the beginning of rotation 
plus any additional 1-minute collection periods that are required. Voltage 
measurements shall be able to be made continuously throughout the rollover test. 
 
3. 
STODDARD AND ELECTROLYTE COLLECTION CONTAINERS AND 
STOPWATCH 
Containers for the collection of Stoddard solvent and propulsion battery electrolyte 
and a calibrated stopwatch for timing the fluid collection intervals are required. 
Containers for each fluid collected must be labeled before they are photographed. 
For containers containing both Stoddard and electrolyte, the fluids should be 
allowed to separate by specific gravity then measured and photographed. 
 
4. 
OTHER TEST INSTRUMENTATION 
The Contractor shall provide the necessary equipment to permanently record and 
display data. The data shall be included in the final test report and on the electronic 
data media. 
 
5.3. 
ELECTROLYTE SPILLAGE AND ELECTRICAL SHOCK PROTECTION PROCEDURE 
1. 
DATA COLLECTION SET-UP  
a. Remove the key from the keylock and ensure the vehicle is not powered.  
b. Remove barriers to access the propulsion battery module (e.g. seat backs, 
carpet, covers).  
c. Wear high-voltage protection gloves, nonconductive shoes, eye protection 
and any other safety equipment deemed necessary to safely prepare the 
vehicle and conduct the test.  
d. Set the propulsion battery module switch, service plug, or otherwise to the 
“OFF” or depowered, position (See Figure 1E below). Follow any 
Manufacturer instructions provided by the COR. Wait 5 minutes. 
 


## Page 243

Side NCAP Pole - E8 
 
Figure 1E: Examples of Service Switches and Plugs 
 
e. Remove propulsion battery module service cover, or cover that closes the 
battery compartment.  
f. Measure the voltage across the propulsion battery at the appropriate 
terminals, and verify 0 volts.  
g. Measure the voltage between the positive terminal of the propulsion battery 
and the vehicle body, and verify 0 volts.  
h. Measure the voltage between the negative terminal of the propulsion battery 
and the vehicle body, and verify 0 volts.  
i. If any voltage measurements differ from 0 volts, STOP, quarantine vehicle, 
document incident and contact the COTR.  
j. Attach test leads from the propulsion battery, propulsion system, automatic 
propulsion battery disconnect, ground points, and any other points necessary 
on the vehicle such that immediate retrieval of data is possible after an impact 
event and at all times during the static rollover test. 
 
NOTE: If vehicle is equipped with an automatic disconnect physically 
contained within the battery pack system, all voltage measurements 
after impact will be taken from the traction side of the automatic 
disconnect to the vehicle chassis. 
 
If the vehicle utilizes an automatic disconnect that is not physically 
contained within the battery pack system, all post-impact voltage 
measurements are to be made from the battery side of the automatic 
disconnect. Automatic disconnect presence, location, and set-up 
instruction is vehicle-specific, and is available from the COTR.  
 
k. Re-install the propulsion battery module service cover, or otherwise close the 
battery compartment. Take great care to preserve the integrity of the 
connection wiring and propulsion battery hold-downs.  
 
2. 
TEST VEHICLE PREPARATION 
a. Apply paint or other highly visible finish, such as machinist blue, to all 
battery system component attachment fasteners or attachment means (e.g., 
welds), to indicate component movement or separation after the governing 
NCAP barrier test.  
Service Plug – Toyota Prius 
  
Service Switch – Honda Civic 
Service Switch – Ford Escape 


## Page 244

Side NCAP Pole - E9 
b. If the vehicle is equipped with a liquid cooling system, assure that the coolant 
is a different color than the Stoddard solvent in use. 
c. Reset the propulsion battery module switch, service plug, or otherwise to the 
“ON”, or powered, position. Verify proper function of propulsion system.  
d. Charge the propulsion battery system to:  
 
1. The maximum state of charge recommended by the manufacturer, as 
stated in the vehicle Owner’s Manual, or on a label that is permanently 
affixed to the vehicle; 
OR  
2. A state of charge of not less than 95 percent of the maximum capacity of 
the battery system, if the manufacturer has made no recommendation. 
Maximum capacity can be verified by consulting the COR;  
 OR  
3. The maximum practicable state of charge within the normal operating 
range, as specified by the manufacturer, and as indicated by the vehicle’s 
instrumentation, if the batteries are rechargeable only by an energy source 
on the vehicle. Discuss with COR prior to operating the vehicle.  
e. 
Complete Data Sheets No. 305-1 and No. 305-2 in Appendix C. 
f. 
Prepare the test vehicle per the remainder of this test procedure. 
g. 
Document and photograph the test vehicle per the requirements set forth in 
this test procedure. 
 
3. 
ELECTRICAL ISOLATION BASELINE MEASUREMENT 
NOTE: The following measurements are to be made immediately prior to the 
crash test, and should be completed within 15 minutes. 
 
a. Check that the battery system is connected to the vehicle’s propulsion system, 
and the vehicle is in the “ready-to-drive” (propulsion motor(s) activated) 
position. Start Data Sheet No. 305-3 in Appendix C.  
b. Measure the voltage of the propulsion battery as shown in Figure 2E. Before 
any vehicle impact test, verify that Vb is equal to or greater than the nominal 
operating voltage, as specified by the vehicle manufacturer, or as supplied by 
the COR. If Vb is not equal to or greater than the nominal operating voltage, as 
specified by the vehicle manufacturer, or as supplied by the COR, repeat the 
propulsion battery charging Step d of Item 2 Test Vehicle Preparation and 
promptly call the COR for guidance. The voltmeter used in this test measures 
direct current values and has an internal impedance of at least 10MΩ. Record 
the voltage measurement as Vb on Data Sheet No. 305-3 in Appendix C. 
Make certain all voltages are DC. If there is AC voltage on the traction side 
connection, consult the COR for additional guidance.

Side NCAP Pole - E13 
NOTE: If the vehicle is equipped with an automatic disconnect 
physically contained within the battery pack system, all 
voltage measurements after impact will be taken from the 
traction side of the automatic disconnect to the vehicle chassis. 
  
If the vehicle utilizes an automatic disconnect that is not 
physically contained within the battery pack system, all post-
impact voltage measurements are to be made from the battery 
side of the automatic disconnect. Automatic disconnect 
presence, location, and set-up instruction is vehicle specific 
and must be obtained from the COTR. 
 
4. 
ELECTRICAL ISOLATION COMPLIANCE MEASUREMENT 
NOTE: All voltage measurements shall be recorded immediately after the 
governing NCAP barrier impact test, and at the start of each 
increment of 90º, 180º, 270º, and 360º of the FMVSS No. 301 indicant 
static rollover test. 
  
NOTE: If the measured voltage is zero and results in a division by zero, 
record “Zero Volts.” This “zero voltage” condition is considered as 
being compliant.  
  
a. Immediately following the crash test, measure V1, V2, V1 ', and V2 ' voltages per 
Figure 6E with Ro installed and record the values on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in 
Appendix C.  
b. Calculate the electrical isolation value (in ohms) as shown in Figure 5E. 
Record the electrical isolation value as Ri1 on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in 
Appendix C.  
c. Calculate the electrical isolation value (in ohms) as shown in Figure 6E. 
Record the electrical isolation value as Ri2 on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in 
Appendix C. 
d. If Ri1 is less than Ri2 then, divide Ri1 by the nominal operating voltage of the 
propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5E. Record this value as Ri / Vb, on 
Data Sheet No. 305-4 in Appendix C. This value must be equal to or greater 
than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test failure has occurred. 
e. 
If Ri2 is less than Ri1 then, divide Ri2 by the nominal operating voltage of the 
propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5E. Record this value as Ri / Vb, on 
Data Sheet No. 305-4 in Appendix C. This value must be equal to or greater 
than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test failure has occurred. 
f. Visually inspect for electrolyte leakage in the passenger compartment and 
record and photograph findings on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in Appendix C. 
Additional photographs to document such findings should be included per the 
requirements set forth in the Photographic Documentation section in 
Appendix C. 


## Page 249

Side NCAP Pole - E14 
g. Visually inspect for external battery component entry into the occupant 
compartment and record and photograph findings on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in 
Appendix C. 
h. Visually inspect for internal battery component movement in the occupant 
compartment and record and photograph findings on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in 
Appendix C. Additional photographs to document such findings should be 
included per the requirements set forth in the Photographic Documentation 
section in Appendix C. 
i. Photograph the test vehicle per the deliverables outlined in the governing 
NCAP barrier test procedure and in this test procedure and record any 
additional findings in the applicable data sheets.  
j. Prepare the vehicle for the static rollover test by following Section 6 (FMVSS 
No. 301 Indicant Test) of this Appendix. 
 
5. 
STATIC ROLLOVER TEST 
NOTE: When the test vehicle is rotated in a fixture on its longitudinal axis to 
each successive increment of 90o following the side impact NCAP 
test, propulsion battery electrolyte leakage shall not exceed 5 liters. 
 
Additionally, electrical isolation shall not be less than 500 ohms/volt 
throughout the side impact NCAP test or at each 90o increment of the 
static rollover test. 
 
The passenger compartment must be visually checked directly after a barrier 
impact for evidence of electrolyte leakage, battery system component 
intrusion, and retention of interior mounted battery modules. Photographs of 
the propulsion battery system components should be taken before the vehicle 
is placed on the static rollover machine. Any ATDs used for governing NCAP 
test should also be removed. 
  
Do not proceed to the static rollover if there are apparent test failures or test 
anomalies of the NCAP barrier test. The Contractor must conduct a static 
rollover test within 45 minutes after the vehicle impact only after the 
Quicklook Report provides assurance that the vehicle has met the performance 
requirements of the applicable frontal, side MDB, or side pole NCAP barrier 
test, and also the requirements outlined by FMVSS No. 301 and 305 indicant 
tests that must be met prior to the static rollover test. The Contractor must 
keep the test vehicle under constant observation for propulsion battery 
electrolyte leakage during the transition between barrier impact and static 
rollover testing. 
  
After the vehicle impact, any propulsion battery electrolyte leakage shall be 
collected by hand and documented with a real time (24 fps) digital motion 
picture camera. Like FMVSS 301 indicant testing, the "tea cup method" may 
be used to collect electrolyte spillage from any leakage source(s), though 
Contractors are invited to suggest alternative methods for fluid collection. The 


## Page 250

Side NCAP Pole - E15 
collected propulsion battery electrolyte samples can subsequently be measured 
and spillage volume calculated. If the "tea cup method" is used, the test 
personnel must be in position to reach observation points around the test 
vehicle at the instant the vehicle comes to rest after the impact event. If 
possible, the collections of Stoddard solvent, propulsion battery electrolyte, or 
any other fluids should be segregated (if leakage of fluids is present). If it is 
not possible to collect leakage samples separately, provide a collection vessel 
that is adequately sized to collect the leakage mixture and separate by suitable 
means, post-test. Take adequate safeguards when collecting leakage, as it may 
be hazardous.  
  
a. Reference static rollover preparation and procedure from Section 6 (FMVSS 
No. 301 Indicant Test) of this Appendix. 
b. Mount the test vehicle on the static rollover fixture and position at 0o (wheels 
down). 
c. Immediately following the rollover transition of each successive increment of 
90o (e.g. at 90o, 180o, 270o, 360o), perform the following: 
  
NOTE: If measured voltage is zero and results in a division by zero, 
record “Zero Volts.” This “zero voltage” condition is 
considered as being compliant.  
 
i. Measure V1, V2, V1 ', and V2 ' voltages per Figures 3E -6E with Ro 
installed, and record the values on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in Appendix C. 
ii. Calculate the electrical isolation value (in ohms) as shown in Figure 5E. 
Record the electrical isolation value as Ri1 on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in 
Appendix C. 
iii. Calculate the electrical isolation value (in ohms) as shown in Figure 6E. 
Record the electrical isolation value as Ri2 on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in 
Appendix C. 
iv. If Ri1 is less than Ri2 then, divide Ri1 by the nominal operating voltage of 
the propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5E. Record this value as Ri / 
Vb, on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in Appendix C. This value must be equal to 
or greater than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test failure has 
occurred. 
v. If Ri2 is less than Ri1 then, divide Ri2 by the nominal operating voltage of 
the propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5E. Record this value as Ri / 
Vb, on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in Appendix C. This value must be equal to 
or greater than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test failure has 
occurred. 
d. Repeat Step c for increments of 180o, 270o, and 360o. 
 
6. 
POST-ROLLOVER REQUIREMENTS 
a.  After the required tests are completed, the Contractor shall: 
i. Verify all data sheets are complete and take any remaining photographs.  


## Page 251

Side NCAP Pole - E16 
ii. Complete S2 of Appendix C, the Report of Vehicle Condition, including 
a word description of the vehicle’s post-test condition. 
iii. Copy applicable pages of the Vehicle Owner’s Manual for attachment to 
the test reports. 
iv. Remove all instrumentation from vehicle. Return vehicle to its pre-test 
condition and move the test vehicle to a secure area.  
v. Place all original records in a secure and organized file to await test data 
disposition.

DELIBERATIVE PROPOSED DRAFT 
OVERVIEW 
 
Summary.  NHTSA has developed an alteration to the SID-IIsD side impact dummy for the 
installation of an instrumentation package within the dummy’s head.  This alteration improves 
the utility of the dummy as a test tool.  This alteration does not change the dummy in any way 
other than to improve its usability and objectivity.1  This document also describes an alteration to 
the regulatory text that serves to correct a minor error in the qualification procedure for the iliac 
test.   
 
Description of alterations.  The alterations are described below. 
 
I.  Instrumentation for the head assembly.  This alteration involves the installation of an 
instrumentation package consisting of three accelerometers, three redundant accelerometers, and 
three angular rate sensors (ARS) within the head of the dummy.  The optional instrumentation 
provides a means to monitor brain injury potential without otherwise affecting the performance 
of the dummy.  The redundant accelerometers serve as back-ups in case an unexpected 
malfunction occurs in the primary accelerometers.   
 
II. Iliac impact procedure.  This alteration corrects an error in the qualification procedure for the 
iliac test. The horizontal orientation of the impactor specified in the current regulatory text is 
incorrect.   
 
Current SID-IIsD Specifications.  The SID-IIsD is specified in 49 CFR § Part 572 Subpart V.  
This publication contains regulatory text describing the qualification procedures and 
requirements for the dummy.   Subpart V also incorporates several other documents by reference.  
Those documents describe the physical make-up of the dummy, and include a parts list, a set of 
engineering drawings, and a document entitled, “Procedures for Assembly, Disassembly, and 
Inspection.”  These references reside in docket file NHTSA-2009-0002 found on 
www.regulations.gov.  The full document titles and document numbers are: 
 
• Parts/Drawings List, Part 572 Subpart V, SID-IIsD, July 1, 2008, NHTSA-2009-0002, 
document no. 0022. 
 
• Drawings and Specifications for the SID-IIsD Small Female Crash Test Dummy, Part 572 
Subpart V, Rev. H, July 1, 2008, NHTSA-2009-0002, document no. 0024. 
 
• Procedures for Assembly, Disassembly, and Inspection (PADI) of the SID-IIsD Side Impact 
Crash Test Dummy, July 1, 2008, NHTSA-2009-0002, document no. 0023. 
 
Implementation of alterations.  The information presented herein describes how the current 
Subpart V specifications are affected by the alterations.  Corresponding edits to the Subpart V 
engineering drawings, parts list, regulatory text, and PADI are provided to explain how to 
implement the alterations correctly.    
                                                 
1 Technical Report: 3aω head instrumentation package applied to the HIII-5F and SID-IIsD:  Effects on impact 
response and mass properties of the head, National Highway Traffic Safety Administration, May 2018. 
 


## Page 256

Side NCAP Pole - F2 
 
DELIBERATIVE PROPOSED DRAFT 
 
End-users may implement the alterations at their discretion.  Note that the alterations are not 
interrelated, so there is no special need to implement them concurrently.  Either can be 
implemented without implementing the other.     
 
Relevance to Part 572.  This document does not in any way constitute a revision to the 49 CFR § 
Part 572 Subpart V.  Nor does it constitute a change to any of the components that are 
incorporated into Subpart V by reference, which include the parts list, the engineering drawing 
package, and the PADI. This document serves only to describe how Subpart V is affected by the 
alterations.   
 
 
 
 
 


## Page 257

Side NCAP Pole - F3 
 
DELIBERATIVE PROPOSED DRAFT 
I.  INSTRUMENTATION FOR THE HEAD ASSEMBLY 
 
1.  Alterations to the Engineering Drawing Package and Parts List.    
 
a.  New drawings added (see Appendix A): 
 
• DL180-1000, Redundant Accelerometers with ARS, SID-IIsD 
• 180-0212R, Mounting plate, SID-IIsD 
• SA572-S79, ARS/Accelerometer Mounting Block 
• SA572-S4984, Redundant Accel. Stacker 
• SA572-S56, Rev. C, Angular Rate Sensor – 8k 
• SA572-S57, Rev. C, Angular Rate Sensor – 12k 
• SA572-S58, Rev. C, Angular Rate Sensor – 18k 
 
b.  Alterations to existing drawings.   
The following drawings are altered to specify an option to install redundant accelerometers and 
angular rate sensors.  
 
• 180-0000, Rev. H, SID-IIsD, Complete Assembly, Sheet 2. 
• 180-0000, Rev. H, SID-IIsD, Complete Assembly, Part Groupings, Sheet 4.   
• 180-1000, Rev. E, 6 Axis Head Assembly. 
 
2.  Alterations to the Subpart V Regulatory Text. 
 
a. Alterations to §572.200 Test conditions and instrumentation. 
 
Insert new paragraph (e): 
 
(e) Optional angular rate sensors for the head, if installed, have the dimensions and response 
characteristics specified in any of drawings SA572-S56, SA572-S57, or SA572-S58.   
 
Former paragraphs (e) and (f) are incremented to (f) and (g). 
 
Former paragraph (g) is incremented to (h) and revised as follows: 
 
(h)  
(1) Head: 
(i) Accelerations – digitally filtered CFC 1000. 
(ii) Angular velocities – digitally filtered CFC 60. 
 
Former paragraphs (h)-(k) are incremented to (i)-(l).

Rename section 6.1.1:

At the top of page 70, add instructions and new pictures that describe the order of installation for 
the optional head instrumentation as follows: 
 
6.1.2  Optional:  Procedure for installing redundant accelerometers and angular rate 
sensors. 
 
1.  Install six uniaxial piezoresistive accelerometers and three angular rate sensors on the 
ARS/accelerometer mounting block (SA572-S79) as shown in Fig. 122 by following steps a-f 
below  Mount all sensors by following the right hand rule for signal polarity in accordance with 
the SAE J211.  See Appendix A for further details on sensor polarities. 
 
a. The two x-axis accelerometers are installed on the front of the mounting block using one 
redundant accelerometer stacker placed between two accelerometers and secured to the  
mounting block with two 0-80 x 3/8 SHCS. 
 
b. The x-axis ARS is mounted on the rear of the mounting block using two 0-80 x 3/8 SHCS. 
 
c. The two y-axis accelerometers are installed on the left side of the mounting block using one 
redundant accelerometer stacker placed between two accelerometers and secured to the mounting 
block with two 0-80 x 3/8 SHCS. 
 
d. The y-axis ARS is installed on the right side of the mounting block using two 0-80 x 3/8 
SHCS. 
 
e. The two z-axis accelerometers are installed on the top of the mounting block using one 
redundant accelerometer stacker placed between two accelerometers and secured to the mounting 
block with two 0-80 x 3/8 SHCS. 
 
f. The z-axis ARS is installed in a pocket on the underside of the mounting block with the label 
side of the ARS facing up using two 0-80 x 3/8 SHCS. 
 
2.  Install the ARS/accelerometer mounting block (SA572-S79) using two 2-56 x 5/8 SHCS on 
the mounting plate (part no. 180-0212R) as shown in Fig. 123.   
 
3. Install the mounting plate (part no. 180-0212R), on the upper neck load cell (part no. SA572-
S11) using two 10-24 x 7/16 SHCS and two 10-24 x 3/8 BHCS as shown in Fig. 124. Optionally 
it is a possibility that the neck transducer structural replacement, part no. 180-1003, is being used 
in place of the upper neck load cell. Note: the 10-24 x 3/8 BHCS under the x-axis ARS cannot be 
installed or removed with the ARS/accelerometer mounting block (SA572-S79) installed. 
 


## Page 264

Side NCAP Pole - F10 
 
DELIBERATIVE PROPOSED DRAFT 
4. Place the upper neck load cell with the mounting plate in the head, but do not install; leave it 
loose. 
 
5. Complete the installation of the upper neck load cell as described in Section 6.2.1.

DELIBERATIVE PROPOSED DRAFT 
II.  ILIAC IMPACT TEST SPECIFICATION 
 
1.  Alterations to the Engineering Drawing Package and Parts List.    
No alterations to the regulatory text are needed. 
 
2.  Alterations to the Subpart V Regulatory Text. 
 
Orientation of the iliac impactor.  Edit the regulatory text in S572.199(b)(8) describing the iliac 
impact test procedure.  The horizontal orientation of the impactor specified in the current 
regulatory text is incorrect.  As shown in the diagram below, the 88.9 mm (3.50 inch) dimension 
of the probe's impact surface should be aligned vertically, not horizontally.   
 
 
Figure II.1.  Diagram of iliac impact test described in S572.199(b)(8) showing that the 88.9 mm 
face of the impact probe is aligned vertically.   
 
This is an obvious error in the regulatory text.  The probe is shown in the regulatory text in Fig. 
V9A, Iliac Impact, part number 180-9800.  The full engineering drawing of the probe (shown 
below) is found in:  Qualification Procedures for the SID-IIsD Side Impact Crash Test Dummy, 
July 1, 2008. (See online link: https://www.regulations.gov; search under nhtsa-2009-0002-
0016.).  The edit consists entirely of the following change: 
 
S572.199   Pelvis iliac. 
 (b) 
 (8) The dummy is positioned with respect to the impactor such that the longitudinal centerline of 
the impact probe is in line with the longitudinal centerline of the iliac load cell access hole, and 
the 88.9 mm dimension of the probe's impact surface is aligned horizontally vertically. 
 
3.  Alterations to the PADI.   
No alterations to the PADI are needed.
